The Third Method: Specifying Intent (Tahrir al-Murad)
Author presents the third method for the proponent to respond to denial by specifying intent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the dialectical method of tahrir al-murad and apply it to analyze exchanges where the proponent responds to denial by specifying intent.

Core Idea
Specifying intent saves a claim from denial by clarifying its true scope.

In jadal, when the opponent denies the proponent's claim with a definitive proof, the proponent cannot simply ignore the denial. Instead, he can respond by specifying what he really meant—restricting the claim, generalizing it, or clarifying the convention or school he was following. This lesson introduces this third method with three examples from different fields.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim and denial
Read each exchange and identify the proponent's original claim and the opponent's denial. Note the definitive proof (sanad qat'i) the opponent uses.
The denial is often introduced by 'mumtani' or 'la usallim'.
2
Classify the specification type
Determine how the proponent specifies his intent: by restriction (takhsis), generalization (ta'mim), adherence to a specific convention (istilah), or following a particular school (madhhab).
The three examples illustrate madhhab, 'urf, and linguistic meaning respectively.
3
Validate the specification
Check if the specification is legitimate: the proponent must genuinely adhere to the cited school, convention, or linguistic usage. Arbitrary changes are not allowed.
In example A, the proponent genuinely follows the Maliki school.
4
Apply to new scenarios
Given a new dialectical exchange, identify whether the proponent's response qualifies as tahrir al-murad and which type he uses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الطريق الثالثة : أن يحرر المعلّل مراده من الدعوى التي منعها السائل، وذلك بتخصيص، أو تعميم، أو جري على اصطلاح خاص، أو جري على مذهب من المذاهب .
أمثلة :
أ ـ المعلل الفقيه : الماء قليله وكثيره لا ينجسه شيء، إلا ما غلب على لونه، أو طعمه، أو ريحه .
السائل : لا أسلم، كيف وما دون القلتين من الماء ينجس بمجرد ملاقاة النجاسة له؟ (منع مقرون بسند قطعي) .
المعلّل : لقد جريت فيما ذكرت على مذهب مالك رضي الله عنه . (جواب بتحرير المراد من المذهب الذي جرى عليه).
ب ـ المعلّل : كل حيوان ليس له أربعة قوائم فليس بدابة .
السائل : ممنوع، كيف والدابة كل ما يدب على الأرض؟ (منع مقرون بسند قطعي) .
المعلّل : لقد جريت فيما ذكرت على ما اشتهر في العرف . (جواب بتحرير المراد من الاصطلاح الذي جرى عليه).
جـ ـ المعلّل : تجوز الصلاة من غير طهارة .
السائل : لا أسلم، كيف وهي لا تجوز إلا بطهارة، باستثناء فاقد الطهورين؟ (منع مقرون بسند قطعي) .
المعلّل : أردت من الصلاة مطلق الدعاء، ولم أرد الصلاة الخاصة في الاصطلاح الشرعي . (جواب بتحرير المراد من لفظة الصلاة).
The third method: that the proponent specifies his intended meaning from the claim which the opponent denied, by way of restriction, or generalization, or following a specific convention, or following one of the schools. Examples: A) The jurist proponent: Water, little and much of it, nothing makes it impure except what overcomes its color, or taste, or odor. The opponent: I do not concede. How is that when water less than two qullas becomes impure merely by contact with impurity? (a denial coupled with a definitive proof). The proponent: In what I mentioned, I followed the school of Malik, may Allah be pleased with him. (An answer by specifying the intended meaning from the school he followed). B) The proponent: Every animal that does not have four legs is not a dābbah. The opponent: Denied. How is that when a dābbah is everything that crawls on the earth? (a denial coupled with a definitive proof). The proponent: In what I mentioned, I followed what is prevalent in custom. (An answer by specifying the intended meaning from the convention he followed). C) The proponent: Prayer is permissible without purification. The opponent: I do not concede. How is that when it is not permissible except with purification, except for one who lacks the two purifiers? (a denial coupled with a definitive proof). The proponent: I meant by prayer absolute supplication, and I did not mean the specific prayer in the legal convention. (An answer by specifying the intended meaning of the word 'prayer').
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage presents the third method of response for the proponent when his original claim is denied by the opponent. It explains that the proponent can 'specify his intent' (taḥrīr al-murād) regarding the disputed claim. This can be done by: restricting the claim (takhṣīṣ), generalizing it (taʿmīm), aligning it with a specific technical convention (iṣṭilāḥ), or aligning it with a particular legal school (madhhab). Three examples are provided from different contexts. The first example is from fiqh: the proponent claims that water is not impure unless its properties change, but the opponent denies based on the well-known hadith about less than two qullas. The proponent responds that he was following the Maliki school. The second example is lexical: the proponent defines 'dābbah' as an animal with four legs, but the opponent counters with the linguistic definition of anything that crawls. The proponent resorts to the common custom (ʿurf). The third example is about prayer: the proponent says prayer is valid without purification, the opponent denies citing the legal requirement. The proponent clarifies he meant 'supplication' (duʿāʾ) linguistically, not the ritual prayer. This method shows how the proponent can avoid being refuted by clarifying the context of his statement.

Key Terms
تحرير المراد
منع
سند قطعي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example about dābbah, what specification did the proponent use?
A) He relied on a specific madhhab.
B) He relied on common custom ('urf).
C) He restricted the claim to four-legged animals.
D) He generalized the claim to all animals.

Key Takeaway
Specifying intent (tahrir al-murad) is a legitimate dialectical move that saves a claim from refutation by revealing its underlying context.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Analyze the following exchange: Proponent: 'Every intoxicant is forbidden.' Opponent: 'Denied, because nabidh (date drink) is intoxicating but some jurists permit it.' Apply tahrir al-murad: how could the proponent specify his intent?
?
Construct your own dialectical exchange between a Shafi'i proponent and a Hanafi opponent on the issue of qunoot in Fajr prayer, using tahrir al-murad to resolve a denial.
